{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: as for your index question... so let's assume that you have a table with 10,000 (ten thousand) forum posts, and each post has an \"id\", and you want to find the post with ID == 3350","date":"2017-02-03T15:51:58.512Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"dshulgin2_","message":"yes","date":"2017-02-03T15:52:24.823Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: in most database systems, all the data of a single \"item\" or \"row\" is stored together, so this means that to find the post with ID 3350, you have to go through 3349 other posts first (and all of their data!), until you find the one with ID == 3350","date":"2017-02-03T15:52:36.059Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"which is a lot of data, and this takes a long time","date":"2017-02-03T15:52:44.779Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(this is often called a \"table scan\")","date":"2017-02-03T15:52:53.213Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: now, you can think of an \"index\" as a sort of separate table with pointers","date":"2017-02-03T15:53:04.813Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: so if I create an index on the \"id\" column, it creates a virtual table of sorts, that *only* contains the IDs of posts, and their corresponding position in the table database","date":"2017-02-03T15:53:22.625Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"mizu_no_oto_work","date":"2017-02-03T15:53:53.580Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: now, when I want to look up the post with ID == 3350, I don't need to 'scan' through 3349 other table items, I only need to scan through 3349 other *IDs* in the 'index table', which is much much smaller and therefore faster","date":"2017-02-03T15:53:57.036Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"pathrocle","date":"2017-02-03T15:54:06.445Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: and once I've found it, it will point me at the position in the \"real\" table that contains the data for forum post 3350","date":"2017-02-03T15:54:16.789Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(there are some more optimizations and storage mechanisms that make this even faster, this is just a high-level explanation of the concept)","date":"2017-02-03T15:54:30.097Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2_: does that make sense, and can you see how that makes it faster to look things up by ID?","date":"2017-02-03T15:54:39.671Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"simply because you have to look through less data to find it","date":"2017-02-03T15:54:47.939Z","type":"message"}
